2268

2269 <span class="event-title">

2270Science and the Humanities series: "The Highly Effective Irrationality of Science a conversation with Michael Strevens</span>

2271

2272 <p>

2273<strong>

2274Speaker:</strong>

2275 Michael Strevens<br/>

2276<em>

2277Professor of Philosophy, New York University</em>

2278<p>

2279

2280 <div id="event-information-41501" class="collapse-content">

2281<p>

2282<span >

2283Modern science has done amazing things. What makes it so powerfuland so different from the attempts to understand nature made by the philosophers and monks of old? In part, its power comes from its ability to draw on and amplify elements of human rationality: logical reasoning, the obligation to provide support for every assertion, a commitment to overcome cultural biases and personal interests. But another part of sciences power, this talk will suggest, derives from an unreasonably close-minded narrowness that channels unprecedented energy into observation and experimentation, achieving a level of focus and commitment to the excavation of empirical detail that would otherwise be unattainable.</span>

2284</p>

2285</div>
